          --mr-toggled-font-family: inherit;

        }
        mr-issue-page[issueClosed] {
          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }
        .container-issue-content {
          padding: 0;
          flex-grow: 1;
          display: flex;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: space-between;
          flex-direction: row;
          flex-wrap: nowrap;
          box-sizing: border-box;
          padding-top: 0.5em;
        }
        .container-outside {
          box-sizing: border-box;
          width: 100%;
          max-width: 100%;
          margin: auto;
          padding: 0;
          display: flex;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: space-between;
          flex-direction: row;
          flex-wrap: no-wrap;
        }
        .container-no-issue {
          padding: 0.5em 16px;
          font-size: var(--chops-large-font-size);
        }
        .metadata-container {
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          background: var(--monorail-metadata-toggled-bg);
          border-right: var(--chops-normal-border);
          border-bottom: var(--chops-normal-border);
          width: 24em;
          min-width: 256px;
          flex-grow: 0;
          flex-shrink: 0;
          box-sizing: border-box;
          z-index: 100;
        }
        .issue-header-container {
          z-index: 10;
          position: sticky;
          top: var(--monorail-header-height);
          margin-bottom: 0.25em;
          width: 100%;
        }
        mr-issue-details {
          min-width: 50%;
          max-width: 1000px;
          flex-grow: 1;
          box-sizing: border-box;
          min-height: 100%;
          padding-left: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);
          padding-right: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);
        }
        mr-issue-metadata {
          position: sticky;
          overflow-y: auto;
          top: var(--monorail-header-height);
          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }
        mr-launch-overview {
          border-left: var(--chops-normal-border);
          padding-left: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);
          padding-right: var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);
          flex-grow: 0;
          flex-shrink: 0;
          width: 50%;

          min-height: 100%;
        }

          .container-issue-content {
            flex-direction: column;
            padding: 0 var(--mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding);
          }
          mr-issue-details, mr-launch-overview {
            width: 100%;

          }
        }
        @media (max-width: 840px) {

            position: static;
          }
        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

<span class="line"><!---->Marking this bug as a blocker for next Beta release.<!----></span>

 documents these details. I found the .zip file at

<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://www.googleapis.com/download/storage/v1/b/chromium-browser-asan/o/win32-release_x64%2Fasan-win32-release_x64-1012368.zip?generation=1654761425936383&amp;alt=media"><!---->https://www.googleapis.com/download/storage/v1/b/chromium-browser-asan/o/win32-release_x64%2Fasan-win32-release_x64-1012368.zip?generation=1654761425936383&amp;alt=media<!----></a>

<span class="line"><!---->As recommended on that page I have tagged this bug with Stability-Memory-AddressSanitizer (docs were wrong but I'm fixing them).<!----></span>

I found the gn args so I should be able to build my own version. The gn args are:



<span class="line"><!---->I found the gn args so I should be able to build my own version. The gn args are:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





dcheck_always_on = false



<span class="line"><!---->dcheck_always_on = false<!----></span>



<br>





enable_ipc_fuzzer = true



<span class="line"><!---->enable_ipc_fuzzer = true<!----></span>



<br>





is_asan = true



<span class="line"><!---->is_asan = true<!----></span>



<br>





is_clang = true



<span class="line"><!---->is_clang = true<!----></span>



<br>





is_component_build = false



<span class="line"><!---->is_component_build = false<!----></span>



<br>





is_debug = false



<span class="line"><!---->is_debug = false<!----></span>



<br>





use_remoteexec = true



<span class="line"><!---->use_remoteexec = true<!----></span>



<br>





v8_enable_verify_heap = true



<span class="line"><!---->v8_enable_verify_heap = true<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I had to replace use_remoteexe=true with use_goma=true.



<span class="line"><!---->I had to replace use_remoteexe=true with use_goma=true.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If this is an incompatibility between Windows and asan I'll have to get the asan team to investigate and recommend fixes. I haven't yet found out who that would be.



<span class="line"><!---->If this is an incompatibility between Windows and asan I'll have to get the asan team to investigate and recommend fixes. I haven't yet found out who that would be.<!----></span>

Some updates:



<span class="line"><!---->Some updates:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I could not reproduce this on Windows 10 21H2.



<span class="line"><!---->I could not reproduce this on Windows 10 21H2.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I don't understand why the call stack from when this bug was filed has no relationship to the call stacks in the clusterfuzz repro. These seem like unrelated bugs. Which one is this bug supposed to be tracking?



<span class="line"><!---->I don't understand why the call stack from when this bug was filed has no relationship to the call stacks in the clusterfuzz repro. These seem like unrelated bugs. Which one is this bug supposed to be tracking?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The clusterfuzz repro is caused by the GPU process crashing repeatedly with access violations. Unfortunately we don't have call stacks or any information for these crashes, so we are flying blind.



<span class="line"><!---->The clusterfuzz repro is caused by the GPU process crashing repeatedly with access violations. Unfortunately we don't have call stacks or any information for these crashes, so we are flying blind.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Given all this is it is not at all clear that this is an asan problem. It may well be a bug in Chrome's GPU process code. Given that I can't reproduce the issue and given my lack of expertise with asan and given the lack of call stacks for the GPU process I'm not sure I can do any more here.



<span class="line"><!---->Given all this is it is not at all clear that this is an asan problem. It may well be a bug in Chrome's GPU process code. Given that I can't reproduce the issue and given my lack of expertise with asan and given the lack of call stacks for the GPU process I'm not sure I can do any more here.<!----></span>

Can you comment on the different call stacks in this bug and in the clusterfuzz link in 



<span class="line"><!---->Can you comment on the different call stacks in this bug and in the clusterfuzz link in <!----></span>





comment#4



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c4"><!---->comment#4<!----></a>





? The crash that you are seeing seems unrelated to the clusterfuzz failure, which is GPU process related. If the clusterfuzz bug is an issue then somebody should open a separate bug for it. I'm not sure why it got conflated with this one.



<span class="line"><!---->? The crash that you are seeing seems unrelated to the clusterfuzz failure, which is GPU process related. If the clusterfuzz bug is an issue then somebody should open a separate bug for it. I'm not sure why it got conflated with this one.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If you put the x64 version of windbg in your path and put "windbg -c "sxd av;g" " in front of chrome.exe on the command line you should get call stacks and more information. Among other things you can save and share a minidump of the crash, with this command: ".dump /miup c:\src\temp\asandump.dmp". When running under windbg you'll need to increase the timeout because Chrome will run more slowly. Doing this might get us a bit more information. In particular it would make it easier to determine where the stray pointer is coming from. The ".dump /ma" command in windbg will produce a full minidump, which would give us even more information, but the resulting file would be much larger.



<span class="line"><!---->If you put the x64 version of windbg in your path and put "windbg -c "sxd av;g" " in front of chrome.exe on the command line you should get call stacks and more information. Among other things you can save and share a minidump of the crash, with this command: ".dump /miup c:\src\temp\asandump.dmp". When running under windbg you'll need to increase the timeout because Chrome will run more slowly. Doing this might get us a bit more information. In particular it would make it easier to determine where the stray pointer is coming from. The ".dump /ma" command in windbg will produce a full minidump, which would give us even more information, but the resulting file would be much larger.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





But, most importantly, I tested this on 21H2 (19044). The bug does not repro for me. Therefore I think it is incorrect to state that this bug is related to Windows versions. There appears to be some other factor that determines whether or not the crash happens. I don't know what that factor is. It might be an asan bug, or it might be a Chrome bug. We don't know.

We don't know.<!----></span>

It's too bad that the asan builder doesn't run the source indexing step. The lack of that step makes it harder to see the right source code for the build, but it does work, with a few manual steps.



<span class="line"><!---->It's too bad that the asan builder doesn't run the source indexing step. The lack of that step makes it harder to see the right source code for the build, but it does work, with a few manual steps.<!----></span>

Looking at 1.dump I see that it crashed in WaitForWork after a call to MsgWaitForMultipleObjectsEx. The source-code is:



<span class="line"><!---->Looking at 1.dump I see that it crashed in WaitForWork after a call to MsgWaitForMultipleObjectsEx. The source-code is:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  void WaitForWork(WaitableEvent* wake_up_event) override {



<span class="line"><!---->  void WaitForWork(WaitableEvent* wake_up_event) override {<!----></span>



<br>





    DCHECK(wake_up_event);



<span class="line"><!---->    DCHECK(wake_up_event);<!----></span>



<br>





    const TimeDelta sleep_time = GetSleepTimeout();



<span class="line"><!---->    const TimeDelta sleep_time = GetSleepTimeout();<!----></span>



<br>





    const DWORD milliseconds_wait = checked_cast<DWORD>(



<span class="line"><!---->    const DWORD milliseconds_wait = checked_cast&lt;DWORD&gt;(<!----></span>



<br>





        sleep_time.is_max() ? INFINITE : sleep_time.InMilliseconds());



<span class="line"><!---->        sleep_time.is_max() ? INFINITE : sleep_time.InMilliseconds());<!----></span>



<br>





    const HANDLE wake_up_event_handle = wake_up_event->handle();



<span class="line"><!---->    const HANDLE wake_up_event_handle = wake_up_event-&gt;handle();<!----></span>



<br>





    MsgWaitForMultipleObjectsEx(1, &wake_up_event_handle, milliseconds_wait,



<span class="line"><!---->    MsgWaitForMultipleObjectsEx(1, &amp;wake_up_event_handle, milliseconds_wait,<!----></span>



<br>





                                QS_ALLINPUT, 0);



<span class="line"><!---->                                QS_ALLINPUT, 0);<!----></span>



<br>





  }



<span class="line"><!---->  }<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The crash happens on this line of assembly language after the call:



<span class="line"><!---->The crash happens on this line of assembly language after the call:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  00007ffa`c253c4a0 41c6443d08f8    mov     byte ptr [r13+rdi+8],0F8h ds:000003c9`4639c168=??



<span class="line"><!---->  00007ffa`c253c4a0 41c6443d08f8    mov     byte ptr [r13+rdi+8],0F8h ds:000003c9`4639c168=??<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It looks to me like this line (and the one that follows) are updating the shadow bytes. That can be confirmed by noting this instruction from the prologue:



<span class="line"><!---->It looks to me like this line (and the one that follows) are updating the shadow bytes. That can be confirmed by noting this instruction from the prologue:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  00007ffa`c253c330 4c8b2d29e82616  mov     r13,qword ptr [chrome!__asan_shadow_memory_dynamic_address (00007ffa`d87aab60)]



<span class="line"><!---->  00007ffa`c253c330 4c8b2d29e82616  mov     r13,qword ptr [chrome!__asan_shadow_memory_dynamic_address (00007ffa`d87aab60)]<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Since the crash dump isn't a full dump the value of chrome!__asan_shadow_memory_dynamic_address is not recorded but the value in r13 looks plausible (64-KB aligned), as we can see in the register values:



<span class="line"><!---->Since the crash dump isn't a full dump the value of chrome!__asan_shadow_memory_dynamic_address is not recorded but the value in r13 looks plausible (64-KB aligned), as we can see in the register values:<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->0:009&gt; r<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->chrome!base::internal::`anonymous namespace'::WorkerThreadCOMDelegate::WaitForWork+0x1a0:<!----></span>

However when I run !vadump it says that there are only 768 bytes (0x300) allocated at that address, which doesn't seem like enough for shadow bytes:



<span class="line"><!---->However when I run !vadump it says that there are only 768 bytes (0x300) allocated at that address, which doesn't seem like enough for shadow bytes:<!----></span>

However I also noticed that this instruction:



<span class="line"><!---->However I also noticed that this instruction:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





  00007ffa`c253c446 41c6443d0800    mov     byte ptr [r13+rdi+8],0



<span class="line"><!---->  00007ffa`c253c446 41c6443d0800    mov     byte ptr [r13+rdi+8],0<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





executed before the crash happened. Since r13 and rdi don't change in-between it seems like the only way that the crash could happen would be if r13 or rdi were not preserved by MsgWaitForMultipleObjectsEx, but that would violate the x64 ABI.



<span class="line"><!---->executed before the crash happened. Since r13 and rdi don't change in-between it seems like the only way that the crash could happen would be if r13 or rdi were not preserved by MsgWaitForMultipleObjectsEx, but that would violate the x64 ABI.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>
